	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Oldham</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Oldham&amp;params=53.5444_N_2.1169_W_region:GB_type:city(96555)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°32′40″N</span> <span class="longitude">2°07′01″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.5444°N 2.1169°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.5444; -2.1169</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Oldham&amp;params=53.5444_N_2.1169_W_region:GB_type:city(96555)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°32′40″N</span> <span class="longitude">2°07′01″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.5444°N 2.1169°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.5444; -2.1169</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Oldham</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span> is a town in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>, England,<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> amid the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> and between the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Irk" title="River Irk">Irk</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Medlock" title="River Medlock">Medlock</a>, 5.3 miles (8.5&#160;km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Rochdale" title="Rochdale">Rochdale</a> and 6.9 miles (11.1&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>. It is the administrative centre of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a>, which had a population of 230,800 in 2015.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">Historically</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>, and with little <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Britain" title="Early modern Britain">early history</a> to speak of, Oldham rose to prominence in the 19th century as an international centre of <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacture_during_the_Industrial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Textile manufacture during the Industrial Revolution">textile manufacture</a>. It was a <a href="/wiki/Boomtown" title="Boomtown">boomtown</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and among the first ever <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialised</a> towns, rapidly becoming "one of the most important centres of cotton and textile industries in England".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOBC1973_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOBC1973-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> At its zenith, it was the most productive <a href="/wiki/Spinning_(textiles)" title="Spinning (textiles)">cotton spinning</a> <a href="/wiki/Mill_town" title="Mill town">mill town</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> producing more cotton than France and Germany combined.<sup id="cite_ref-Contaminated_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Contaminated-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Oldham's textile industry fell into decline in the mid-20th century; the town's last mill closed in 1998.
</p><p>The demise of textile processing in Oldham depressed and heavily affected the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Evolution_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Evolution-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Today Oldham is a predominantly residential town, and the improvement of the town centre is the focus of a project for transforming Oldham into a centre for <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It is, however, still distinguished architecturally by the surviving <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">cotton mills</a> and other buildings associated with that industry.  As of 2001, the town had a population of <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_England_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of urban areas in England by population">103,544</a><sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Population_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Population-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and an area of around 26 square miles (67&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oldham" title="History of Oldham">History of Oldham</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a> of Oldham seems to imply "old village or place" from <i>Eald</i> (<a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon language">Saxon</a>) signifying oldness or antiquity, and <i>Ham</i> (Saxon) a house, farm or <a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(place)" title="Hamlet (place)">hamlet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Oldham is however known to be a derivative of <i>Aldehulme</i>, undoubtedly an <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> name.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It is believed to be derived from the <a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a> <i>ald</i> combined with the Old Norse <i>holmi</i> or <i>holmr</i>, meaning "promontory or outcrop", possibly describing the town's hilltop position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It has alternatively been suggested that it may mean "holm or hulme of a farmer named Alda".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The name is understood to date from 865, during the period of the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cumbric" title="Cumbric">Cumbric</a> <i>alt</i>, meaning "steep height, cliff", has also been suggested for the first element.<sup id="cite_ref-bliton_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bliton-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The earliest known evidence of a human presence in what is now Oldham is attested by the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> flint arrow-heads and workings found at <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a> and Besom Hill, implying habitation 7–10,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Evidence of later <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> activity is confirmed by an ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman road">Roman road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> archaeological relics found at various sites within the town.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Placenames of Celtic origin are still to be found in Oldham: Werneth derives from a Celtic personal name identical to the <a href="/wiki/Gaulish" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaulish">Gaulish</a> <i>vernetum</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Alder" title="Alder">alder</a> swamp",<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Glodwick" title="Glodwick">Glodwick</a> may be related to the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Welsh" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Welsh">modern Welsh</a> <i>clawdd</i>, meaning "dyke" or "ditch".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson19493_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson19493-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Nearby <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a> is also pre-Anglo-Saxon in origin, from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Welsh" title="Old Welsh">Old Welsh</a> <i>cadeir</i>, itself deriving from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>cathedra</i> meaning "chair".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMills197639_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMills197639-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  Although <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a> occupied territory around the area centuries earlier,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBallard1986_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBallard1986-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Oldham as a permanent, named place of dwelling is believed to date from 865, when <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danish invaders</a> established a settlement called Aldehulme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaly1974_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaly1974-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From its founding in the 9th century until the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, Oldham is believed to have been little more than a scattering of small and insignificant settlements spread across the <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> and dirt tracks that linked <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> to <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Although not mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a>, Oldham does appear in legal documents from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, invariably recorded as territory under the control of minor <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">ruling families</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baron" title="Baron">barons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaly1974_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaly1974-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In the 13th century, Oldham was documented as a manor held from <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a> by a family surnamed <a href="/wiki/Oldham_(surname)" title="Oldham (surname)">Oldham</a>, whose seat was at <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Richard de Oldham was recorded as <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_manor" title="Lord of the manor">lord of the manor</a> of Werneth/Oldham (1354). His daughter and heiress, Margery (d.1384), married John de Cudworth (d.1384), from whom descended the Cudworths of Werneth Hall who were successive lords of the manor. A Member of this family was <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James I</a>'s Chaplain <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Cudworth_(died_1624)" title="Ralph Cudworth (died 1624)">Ralph Cudworth</a> (father of the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Platonists" title="Cambridge Platonists">Cambridge Platonist</a> philosopher <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Cudworth" title="Ralph Cudworth">Ralph Cudworth</a>). The Cudworths remained lords of the manor until their sale of the estate (1683) to <a href="/wiki/Sir_Ralph_Assheton,_2nd_Baronet,_of_Middleton" title="Sir Ralph Assheton, 2nd Baronet, of Middleton">Sir Ralph Assheton</a> of <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Middleton, Greater Manchester">Middleton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution_and_cotton">Industrial Revolution and cotton</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Industrial Revolution and cotton">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_From_Glodwick.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_From_Glodwick.png/220px-Oldham_From_Glodwick.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_From_Glodwick.png/330px-Oldham_From_Glodwick.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_From_Glodwick.png/440px-Oldham_From_Glodwick.png 2x" data-file-width="1683" data-file-height="1071" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_From_Glodwick.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Oldham from <a href="/wiki/Glodwick" title="Glodwick">Glodwick</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/James_Howe_Carse" title="James Howe Carse">James Howe Carse</a> (1831), depicts the early skyline and industrial activities of Oldham. All the <a href="/wiki/Open_space_reserve" title="Open space reserve">green space</a> has since been <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanised</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Much of Oldham's history is concerned with <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacture_during_the_Industrial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Textile manufacture during the Industrial Revolution">textile manufacture during the Industrial Revolution</a>; it has been said that "if ever the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> placed a town firmly and squarely on the map of the world, that town is Oldham."<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Evolution_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Evolution-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Oldham's soils were too thin and poor to sustain <a href="/wiki/Crop" title="Crop">crop</a> growing, and so for decades prior to <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a> the area was used for grazing <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a>, which provided the raw material for a local <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">woollen</a> weaving trade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1756, Oldham had emerged as centre of the <a href="/wiki/Hatter" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatter">hatting</a> industry in England. The rough <a href="/wiki/Felt" title="Felt">felt</a> used in the production process is the origin of the term "Owdham Roughyed" a <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">nickname</a> for people from Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was not until the last quarter of the 18th century that Oldham changed from being a <a href="/wiki/Cottage_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cottage industry">cottage industry</a> township producing woollen garments via domestic <a href="/wiki/Manual_labour" title="Manual labour">manual labour</a>, to a sprawling industrial metropolis of textile factories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The climate, geology, and topography of Oldham were unrelenting constraints upon the social and economic activities of the human inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKidd1977_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKidd1977-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> At 700 feet (213&#160;m) above sea level and with no major river or visible natural resources, Oldham had poor geographic attributes compared with other settlements for investors and their engineers. As a result, Oldham played no part in the initial period of the Industrial Revolution,<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> although it did later become seen as obvious territory to industrialise because of its convenient position between the labour forces of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and southwest <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoster1974_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoster1974-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">Cotton</a> <a href="/wiki/Spinning_(textiles)" title="Spinning (textiles)">spinning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">milling</a> were introduced to Oldham when its first mill, Lees Hall, was built by William Clegg in about 1778, the beginning of a spiralling process of <a href="/wiki/Urbanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Urbanisation">urbanisation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">socioeconomic</a> transformation.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Within a year, 11 other mills had been constructed,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and by 1818 there were 19&#160;– not a large number in comparison with other local settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Oldham's small local population was greatly increased by the mass migration of workers from outlying villages,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a population increase from just over 12,000 in 1801 to 137,000 in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The speed of this urban growth meant that Oldham, with little pre-industrial history to speak of, was effectively born as a <a href="/wiki/Mill_town" title="Mill town">factory town</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royd_Mill,_Hollinwood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Royd_Mill%2C_Hollinwood.jpg/220px-Royd_Mill%2C_Hollinwood.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Royd_Mill%2C_Hollinwood.jpg/330px-Royd_Mill%2C_Hollinwood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Royd_Mill%2C_Hollinwood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="393" data-file-height="536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royd_Mill,_Hollinwood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royd mill, built in 1907,<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and seen here in 1983, was one of the more than 360 textile mills that operated night and day during Oldham's peak.</div></div></div>
<p>Oldham became the world's manufacturing centre for cotton spinning in the second half of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1851, over 30% of Oldham's population was employed within the textile sector, compared to 5% across Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoster1974_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoster1974-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It overtook the major urban centres of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolton" title="Bolton">Bolton</a> as the result of a mill building boom in the 1860s and 1870s, a period during which Oldham became the most productive cotton-spinning town in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1871, Oldham had more <a href="/wiki/Cotton-spinning_machinery" title="Cotton-spinning machinery">spindles</a> than any country in the world except the United States, and in 1909, was spinning more cotton than France and Germany combined.<sup id="cite_ref-Contaminated_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Contaminated-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> By 1911 there were 16.4&#160;million spindles in Oldham, compared with a total of 58&#160;million in the United Kingdom and 143.5&#160;million in the world; in 1928, with the construction of the UK's largest textile factory Oldham reached its manufacturing zenith.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> At its peak, there were more than 360 mills, operating night and day;<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Spinning_Web_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Spinning_Web-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham's townscape was dominated by distinctive rectangular brick-built mills.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESellers199147_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESellers199147-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Oldham was hit hard by the <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_Cotton_Famine" title="Lancashire Cotton Famine">Lancashire Cotton Famine</a> of 1861–1865, when supplies of raw cotton from the United States were cut off. Wholly reliant upon the textile industry, the cotton famine created chronic unemployment in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillett1996_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillett1996-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> By 1863 a committee had been formed, and with aid from central government, land was purchased with the intention of employing local cotton workers to construct <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Park,_Oldham" title="Alexandra Park, Oldham">Alexandra Park</a>, which opened on 28 August 1865.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillett1996_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillett1996-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Said to have over-relied upon the textile sector,<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Evolution_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Evolution-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaly1974_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaly1974-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> as the importation of cheaper foreign <a href="/wiki/Yarn" title="Yarn">yarns</a> grew during the 20th century, Oldham's economy declined into a depression, although it was not until 1964 that Oldham ceased to be the largest centre of cotton spinning.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Evolution_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Evolution-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClough1996_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClough1996-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In spite of efforts to increase the efficiency and competitiveness of its production, the last cotton spun in the town was in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Engineering">Engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Facilitated by its flourishing textile industry, Oldham developed extensive <a href="/wiki/Structural_engineering" title="Structural engineering">structural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> sectors during the 18th and 19th centuries. The manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Cotton-spinning_machinery" title="Cotton-spinning machinery">spinning and weaving machinery</a> in Oldham belongs to the last decade of the 19th century, when it became a leading centre in the field of <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Platt_Brothers" title="Platt Brothers">Platt Brothers</a>, originated in nearby <a href="/wiki/Dobcross" title="Dobcross">Dobcross</a> village, but moved to Oldham. They were pioneers of cotton-spinning machinery, developing innovative products that enabled the mass-production of cotton yarn. Platt Brothers became the largest textile machine makers in the world, employing over 15,000 people in the 1890s,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> twice the number of their nearest rivals Dobson &amp; Barlow in Bolton and Asa Lees on <a href="/wiki/Greenacres,_Greater_Manchester" title="Greenacres, Greater Manchester">Greenacres Moor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Spinning_Web_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Spinning_Web-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> They were keen investors in the local area and at one time, were supporting 42% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The centre of the company lay at the New Hartford Works in <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a>, a massive complex of buildings and internal railways on a site overlooking Manchester. The railway station which served this site later formed the basis of <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Werneth_railway_station" title="Oldham Werneth railway station">Oldham Werneth railway station</a>.  The main building exists to this day. Platts gained prestigious awards from around the world,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillett1996_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillett1996-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and were heavily involved with local politics and civic pride in Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> John and James Platt were the largest subscribers for promoting Oldham from a township to a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">Borough</a>, pledging £100 (more than double the next largest sum) in advance towards any expenses which may have been incurred by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1854 <a href="/wiki/John_Platt_(MP)" title="John Platt (MP)">John Platt</a> was made the (fourth) Mayor of Oldham, an office he was to hold twice more in 1855–56 and 1861–62.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastham1994_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastham1994-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> John Platt was elected in 1865 to become <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> for <a href="/wiki/Oldham_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oldham (UK Parliament constituency)">Oldham</a>, and was re-elected in 1868; he remained in office until his death in 1872.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A bronze statue of Platt existed in the town centre for years, though was moved to <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Park,_Oldham" title="Alexandra Park, Oldham">Alexandra Park</a>. There have been recommendations for it to be returned to the town centre.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Abraham Henthorn Stott, the son of a <a href="/wiki/Stonemason" class="mw-redirect" title="Stonemason">stonemason</a>, was born in nearby <a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Shaw and Crompton</a> in 1822.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He served a seven-year apprenticeship with <a href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_Barry" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Charles Barry">Sir Charles Barry</a>, before starting a structural engineering practice in Oldham in 1847 that went on to become the pre-eminent mill architect firm in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Philip Sydney Stott, third son of Abraham and later titled as <a href="/wiki/Sir_Philip_Stott,_1st_Baronet" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Philip Stott, 1st Baronet">Sir Philip Stott, 1st Baronet</a>, was the most prominent and famous of the Stott mill architects.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He established his own practice in 1883 and designed over a hundred mills in several countries. His factories, which improved upon his father's <a href="/wiki/Fireproofing" title="Fireproofing">fireproof</a> mills, accounted for a 40% increase in Oldham's spindles between 1887 and 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although textile-related engineering declined with the processing industry, leading to the demise of both Stotts and Platts, other engineering firms existed, notably electrical and later electronic engineers <a href="/wiki/Ferranti" title="Ferranti">Ferranti</a> in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Spinning_Web_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Spinning_Web-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Ferranti went into receivership in 1993, but some of its former works continue in other hands. Part of the original <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> site was operated by <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens</a> Metering and Semiconductor divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Spinning_Web_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Spinning_Web-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The remainder of the site is occupied by Mirror Colour Print Ltd; the printing division of the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a> group, which prints and distributes thirty-six major newspapers, and employs five hundred staff.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coal_mining">Coal mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Coal mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On the back of the Industrial Revolution, Oldham developed an extensive coal mining sector, correlated to supporting the local cotton industry and the town's inhabitants, though there is evidence of small scale coal mining in the area as early as the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Coalfield" title="Oldham Coalfield">Oldham Coalfield</a> stretched from <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Bardsley,_Greater_Manchester" title="Bardsley, Greater Manchester">Bardsley</a> in the south and in addition to Oldham, included the towns of <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Middleton, Greater Manchester">Middleton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a> to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Oldham Coalfield was the site of over 150 collieries during its <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Although some contemporary sources suggest there was coal mining in Oldham at a commercial scale by 1738,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> older sources attribute the commercial expansion of coal mining with the arrival in the town of two <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> labourers, John Evans and William Jones, around 1770.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Foreseeing the growth in demand for coal as a source of motive and steam power, they acquired colliery rights for Oldham, which by 1771 had 14 colliers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The mines were largely to the southwest of the town around <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a> and provided enough coal to accelerate Oldham's rapid development at the centre of the cotton boom. At its height in the mid-19th century, when it was dominated by the Lees and Jones families, Oldham coal was mainly sourced from many small collieries whose lives varied from a few years to many decades, although two of the four largest collieries survived to <a href="/wiki/National_Coal_Board" title="National Coal Board">nationalisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFanning2001_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFanning2001-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In 1851, collieries employed more than 2,000 men in Oldham,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFanning2001_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFanning2001-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> although the amount of coal in the town was somewhat overestimated however, and production began to decline even before that of the local spinning industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Today, the only visible remnants of the mines are disused shafts and boreholes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadin2006_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadin2006-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_history">Social history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Social history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg/220px-MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg/330px-MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="266" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MandK_Industrial_Revolution_1900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Workmen leaving <a href="/wiki/Platt_Brothers" title="Platt Brothers">Platt's Works</a>, Oldham, 1900</div></div></div>
<p>Oldham's <a href="/wiki/Social_history" title="Social history">social history</a>, like that of other former <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Franchise_in_the_United_Kingdom_1885-1918" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary Franchise in the United Kingdom 1885-1918">unenfranchised</a> towns, is marked by politicised <a href="/wiki/Civil_disturbance" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil disturbance">civil disturbances</a>, as well as events related to the <a href="/wiki/Luddite" title="Luddite">Luddite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suffragette" title="Suffragette">Suffragette</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">Labour movements</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working classes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  There has been a significant presence of "<a href="/wiki/Friendly_society" title="Friendly society">friendly societies</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> It has been put that the people of Oldham became radical in politics in the early part of the 19th century, and movements suspected of <a href="/wiki/Sedition" title="Sedition">sedition</a> found patronage in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Oldham was frequently disturbed by bread and labour riots, facilitated by periods of scarcity and the disturbance of employment following the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Cotton-spinning_machinery" title="Cotton-spinning machinery">cotton-spinning machinery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April 1812, a "large crowd of riotous individuals" compelled local retailers to sell foods at a loss, whilst on the same day <a href="/wiki/Luddites" class="mw-redirect" title="Luddites">Luddites</a> numbering in their thousands, many of whom were from Oldham, attacked a cotton mill in nearby <a href="/wiki/Middleton,_Greater_Manchester" title="Middleton, Greater Manchester">Middleton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> On 16 August 1819, Oldham sent a contingent estimated at well above 10,000 to hear speakers in St Peter's Fields at Manchester discuss political reform;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPhillips197723_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPhillips197723-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> it was the largest contingent sent to Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarlow1969120_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarlow1969120-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> John Lees, a cotton operative and ex-soldier who had fought at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Waterloo</a>, was one of the fifteen victims of the <a href="/wiki/Peterloo_Massacre" title="Peterloo Massacre">Peterloo Massacre</a> which followed. The 'Oldham inquest' which proceeded the massacre was anxiously watched; the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_King%27s_Bench" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of King&#39;s Bench">Court of King's Bench</a>, however, decided that the proceedings were irregular, and the jury were discharged without giving a verdict.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Annie_Kenney" title="Annie Kenney">Annie Kenney</a>, born in nearby <a href="/wiki/Springhead,_Greater_Manchester" title="Springhead, Greater Manchester">Springhead</a>, and who worked in Oldham's cotton mills, was a notable member of the <a href="/wiki/Suffragette" title="Suffragette">Suffragette</a> movement credited with sparking off suffragette militancy when she heckled <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, and later (with <a href="/wiki/Emmeline_Pankhurst" title="Emmeline Pankhurst">Emmeline Pankhurst</a>) the first <a href="/wiki/Suffragist" class="mw-redirect" title="Suffragist">Suffragist</a> to be imprisoned. Oldham Women's Suffrage Society was established in 1910 with Margery Lees as president and quickly joined the Manchester and District Federation of the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Women%27s_Suffrage_Societies" title="National Union of Women&#39;s Suffrage Societies">National Union of Women's Suffrage Societies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrawford2000_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrawford2000-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chartism" title="Chartism">Chartist</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_cooperative_movement" title="History of the cooperative movement">Co-operative movements</a> had strong support in the town, whilst many Oldhamers protested in support of the emancipation of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Riot_Act" title="Riot Act">Riot Act</a> was read in <a href="/wiki/1852_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1852 United Kingdom general election">1852 on election day</a> following a mass public brawl over the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Act" title="Reform Act">Reform Act</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-OSD_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSD-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and irregularities with parliamentary candidate nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For three days in late May 2001, Oldham became the centre of national and international media attention. Following high-profile <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">race-related</a> conflicts, and long-term underlying racial tensions between local <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistani" class="mw-redirect" title="British Pakistani">British Pakistani</a> communities, major riots broke out in the town. Occurring with particular intensity in the <a href="/wiki/Glodwick" title="Glodwick">Glodwick</a> area of the town, the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldham riots">Oldham riots</a> were the worst racially motivated riots in the United Kingdom for fifteen years prior, briefly eclipsing the sectarian violence in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> in the media.<sup id="cite_ref-Ritchie_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ritchie-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> At least 20 people were injured in the riots, including 15 police officers, and 37 people were arrested. Similar riots took place in other towns in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">northern England</a> over the following days and weeks. The 2001 riots prompted governmental and independent inquiries, which collectively agreed on community relations improvements and considerable regeneration schemes for the town.<sup id="cite_ref-Ritchie_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ritchie-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cantle_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cantle-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>  There were further fears of riots after the death of Gavin Hopley in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_history">Civic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Civic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png/220px-Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png/330px-Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png/440px-Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png 2x" data-file-width="443" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_County_Borough_Council_-_coat_of_arms2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of the former <a href="/wiki/County_Borough_of_Oldham" title="County Borough of Oldham">County Borough of Oldham</a> council, granted 7 November 1894, based upon those of an ancient local family <a href="/wiki/Oldham_(surname)" title="Oldham (surname)">surnamed Oldham</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Owls" class="mw-redirect" title="Owls">owls</a> suggest that the family, like the town, called itself 'Owdham', and adopted the birds in allusion to its name. The motto <i>"Sapere aude"</i> ("Dare to be wise") refers to the owls.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Lying within the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">historic county boundaries</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lancashire" title="History of Lancashire">since the early 12th century</a>, Oldham was recorded in 1212 as being one of five parts of the <a href="/wiki/Thegn" title="Thegn">thegnage</a> estate of Kaskenmoor, which was held on behalf of <a href="/wiki/John_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="John of England">King John</a> by <a href="/wiki/Roger_de_Montbegon" title="Roger de Montbegon">Roger de Montbegon</a> and William de Nevill.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The other parts of this estate were <a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Crompton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glodwick" title="Glodwick">Glodwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sholver" title="Sholver">Sholver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBallard1986_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBallard1986-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Oldham later formed a <a href="/wiki/Township_(England)" title="Township (England)">township</a> within the ancient ecclesiastical parish of <a href="/wiki/Prestwich-cum-Oldham" title="Prestwich-cum-Oldham">Prestwich-cum-Oldham</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Salford_(hundred)" class="mw-redirect" title="Salford (hundred)">hundred of Salford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1826 commissioners for the social and economic improvement of Oldham were established.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The town was made part of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary borough">parliamentary borough</a>, in 1832, though it was in 1849 when Oldham was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">municipal borough</a>, giving it <a href="/wiki/Borough_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Borough status in the United Kingdom">borough status in the United Kingdom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and in 1850 the Borough Council obtained the powers of the improvement commissioners.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 1880, parts of the <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crossbank" title="Crossbank">Crossbank</a> areas of <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashton-under-Lyne" title="Ashton-under-Lyne">Ashton-under-Lyne</a> townships were added to the Borough of Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Above_Town" title="Oldham Above Town">Oldham Above Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Below_Town" title="Oldham Below Town">Oldham Below Town</a> were, from 1851 until c. 1881, statistical units used for the gathering and organising of <a href="/wiki/Civil_registration" title="Civil registration">civil registration</a> information, and output of <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">census</a> data.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a> created elected <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county councils</a> to administer services throughout England and Wales. Where a municipal borough had a population of more than 50,000 at the 1881 <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">Census</a> it was created a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a>, with the powers and duties of both a borough and county council.<sup id="cite_ref-youngs_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngs-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> As Oldham had an 1881 population of 111,343 it duly became a county borough on 1 April 1889. The borough, while independent of Lancashire County Council for local government, remained part of the county for purposes such as the administration of justice and <a href="/wiki/Lord_lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord lieutenant">lieutenancy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1951 parts of the <a href="/wiki/Limehurst_Rural_District" title="Limehurst Rural District">Limehurst Rural District</a> were added to the County Borough of Oldham, and in 1954 further parts of the same district added to it on its abolition.<sup id="cite_ref-youngs_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngs-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Since 1961, Oldham has been <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns">twinned</a> with <a href="/wiki/Kranj" title="Kranj">Kranj</a> in <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>, the town's autonomous county borough status was abolished, and Oldham has, since 1 April 1974, formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_county" title="Metropolitan county">Metropolitan county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Gazetteer_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Gazetteer-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_representation">Parliamentary representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Parliamentary representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The boundaries of two <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">parliamentary constituencies</a> divide Oldham: <a href="/wiki/Oldham_East_and_Saddleworth_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oldham East and Saddleworth (UK Parliament constituency)">Oldham East and Saddleworth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oldham_West_and_Royton_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oldham West and Royton (UK Parliament constituency)">Oldham West and Royton</a> (which includes the town centre), represented by <a href="/wiki/Labour_party_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour party (UK)">Labour</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Members of Parliament</a> <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Abrahams" title="Debbie Abrahams">Debbie Abrahams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_McMahon_(politician)" title="Jim McMahon (politician)">Jim McMahon</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Created as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary borough">parliamentary borough</a> <a href="/wiki/Reform_Act_1832" title="Reform Act 1832">in 1832</a>, Oldham's first parliamentary representatives were the <a href="/wiki/Radicalism_(historical)" title="Radicalism (historical)">radicals</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Cobbett" title="William Cobbett">William Cobbett</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Fielden" title="John Fielden">John Fielden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vision_of_Oldham_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_of_Oldham-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> began his political career in Oldham. Although unsuccessful at his first attempt in 1899, Churchill was elected as the member of Parliament for the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oldham (UK Parliament constituency)">Oldham parliamentary borough constituency</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1900_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1900 United Kingdom general election">1900 general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He held the constituency for the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> until the <a href="/wiki/1906_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1906 United Kingdom general election">1906 general election</a>, when he won the election for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_North_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Manchester North West (UK Parliament constituency)">Manchester North West</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a> MP. After he became the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> in 1940, Churchill was made a <a href="/wiki/Honorary_Freedom_of_Boroughs_Act_1885" title="Honorary Freedom of Boroughs Act 1885">Honorary Freeman of the Borough of Oldham</a>, on 2 April 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>
