<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Oldham.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Map_of_Oldham.png/220px-Map_of_Oldham.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Map_of_Oldham.png/330px-Map_of_Oldham.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Map_of_Oldham.png/440px-Map_of_Oldham.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Oldham.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Oldham, and surrounding area</div></div></div>
<p>At <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Oldham&amp;params=53_32_39_N_2_7_0.8_W_type:city"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°32′39″N</span> <span class="longitude">2°7′0.8″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.54417°N 2.116889°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.54417; -2.116889</span></span></span></a></span> (53.5444°, −2.1169°), and 164 miles (264&#160;km) north-northwest of London, Oldham stands 700 feet (213&#160;m) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>, 6.9 miles (11.1&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">Manchester city centre</a>, on elevated ground between the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Irk" title="River Irk">Irk</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Medlock" title="River Medlock">Medlock</a>. <a href="/wiki/Saddleworth" title="Saddleworth">Saddleworth</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Pennines" title="South Pennines">South Pennines</a> are close to the east, whilst on all other sides, Oldham is bound by smaller towns, including <a href="/wiki/Ashton-under-Lyne" title="Ashton-under-Lyne">Ashton-under-Lyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Failsworth" title="Failsworth">Failsworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Shaw and Crompton</a>, with little or no <a href="/wiki/Green_belt" title="Green belt">green space</a> between them. Oldham experiences a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a>, like much of the British Isles, with relatively cool summers and mild winters. There is regular but generally light precipitation throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKidd1977_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKidd1977-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On 23 November 1981, <a href="/wiki/1981_United_Kingdom_tornado_outbreak" title="1981 United Kingdom tornado outbreak">an F1/T2 tornado</a> formed over <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> and later passed over Oldham town centre, causing some damage.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham's <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a> is characterised by its rugged, <a href="/wiki/Upland_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Upland (geology)">elevated</a> <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennine</a> terrain.<sup id="cite_ref-Cotton_Mills_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotton_Mills-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top_of_England_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_of_England-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> It has an area of 6.91 square miles (17.90&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Population_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Population-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a> of Oldham is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Millstone_Grit" title="Millstone Grit">Millstone Grit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal_Measures" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal Measures">Coal Measures</a> series of rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKidd1977_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKidd1977-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/River_Beal" title="River Beal">River Beal</a>, flowing northwards, forms the boundary between Oldham on one side and <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Shaw and Crompton</a> on the other.
</p><p>To the east of this river the surface rises to a height of 1,225 feet (373&#160;m) at Woodward Hill, on the border with the parish of <a href="/wiki/Saddleworth" title="Saddleworth">Saddleworth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the surface is hilly, the average height decreasing towards the southwest to <a href="/wiki/Failsworth" title="Failsworth">Failsworth</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>. The ridge called Oldham Edge, 800 feet (244&#160;m) high, comes southward from Royton into the centre of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg/200px-Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg/300px-Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg/400px-Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="427" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mill_%26_Church_-_Oldham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oldham's irregularly constructed <a href="/wiki/Built_environment" title="Built environment">built environment</a> is characterised by its red-brick <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">cotton mills</a> and surrounding <a href="/wiki/Terraced_house" title="Terraced house">terraced houses</a>.</div></div></div><p>
Oldham's <a href="/wiki/Built_environment" title="Built environment">built environment</a> is characterised by its 19th-century red-brick <a href="/wiki/Terraced_house" title="Terraced house">terraced houses</a>, the infrastructure that was built to support these and the town's former <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">cotton mills</a>&#160;– which mark the town's skyline.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClough1996_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClough1996-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Urban_structure" title="Urban structure">urban structure</a> of Oldham is irregular when compared to most <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_England" title="List of towns in England">towns in England</a>, its form restricted in places by its hilly upland terrain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownbill191192–108-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top_of_England_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_of_England-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> There are irregularly constructed residential dwellings and streets clustered loosely around a <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Town_centre" title="Town centre">town centre</a>, which is the local centre of commerce. In 1849, Angus Reach of <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> said: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The visitor to Oldham will find it essentially a mean-looking straggling town, built upon both sides and crowning the ridge of one of the outlying spurs which branch from Manchester, the neighbouring 'backbone of England'. The whole place has a shabby underdone look. The general appearance of the operatives' houses is filthy and smouldering.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Angus Reach, <i>Morning Chronicle, 1849</i></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>In the 1870s, <a href="/wiki/John_Marius_Wilson" title="John Marius Wilson">John Marius Wilson</a> described Oldham as consisting of:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>... numerous streets, and contains numerous fine buildings, both public and private; but, in a general view, is irregularly constructed, presents the dingy aspect of a crowded seat of manufacture, and is more notable for factories than for any other feature.<sup id="cite_ref-Vision_of_Oldham_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_of_Oldham-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>John Marius Wilson, <i><a href="/wiki/Imperial_Gazetteer_of_England_and_Wales" title="Imperial Gazetteer of England and Wales">Imperial Gazetteer of England and Wales</a> (1870–1872)</i></cite></div>
</blockquote><p> Although Oldham had a thriving economy during the 19th century, the local merchants were broadly reluctant to spend on civic institutions, and so the town lacks the grandeur seen in comparable nearby towns like <a href="/wiki/Bolton" title="Bolton">Bolton</a> or <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rebrand_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebrand-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> public expenditure was seen as an overhead that undermined the competitiveness of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Oldham's architecture has been described as "mediocre".<sup id="cite_ref-Rebrand_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebrand-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The town has no <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a> with a Grade I rating.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a mixture of high-density <a href="/wiki/Urban_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban areas">urban areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburbs</a>, semi-rural and <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">rural</a> locations in Oldham. There is some permanent <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a> but overwhelmingly the <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a> in the town is urban. The territory of Oldham is contiguous with other towns on all sides except for a small section along its eastern and southern boundaries, and for purposes of the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a>, forms the fourth largest settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Urban_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Manchester Urban Area">Greater Manchester Urban Area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_conurbations_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="List of conurbations in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom's third largest conurbation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/M60_motorway" title="M60 motorway">M60 motorway</a> passes through the southwest of Oldham, through <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Heavy_rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy rail">heavy rail</a> line enters Oldham from the same direction, travelling northeast to the town centre before heading northwards through <a href="/wiki/Derker" title="Derker">Derker</a> towards Shaw and Crompton.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_panorama_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg/800px-Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg/1200px-Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg/1600px-Oldham_panorama_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2046" data-file-height="519" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_panorama_(crop).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>A panorama of Oldham looking from <a href="/wiki/Hartshead_Pike" title="Hartshead Pike">Hartshead Pike</a> toward the north west.</center></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions_and_suburbs">Divisions and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Divisions and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fredrick_Street,_Werneth,_Oldham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg/220px-Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg/330px-Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg/440px-Fredrick_Street%2C_Werneth%2C_Oldham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2063" data-file-height="1543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fredrick_Street,_Werneth,_Oldham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fredrick Street, in <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a>. Much of Oldham's housing stock is two-up-two-down rows of <a href="/wiki/Terraced_house" title="Terraced house">terraced houses</a>, a reminder of its <a href="/wiki/Mill_town" title="Mill town">mill town</a> history.</div></div></div>
<p>Many of Oldham's present divisions and suburbs have origins as pre-industrial hamlets, manorial commons and ancient chapelries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Some, such as <a href="/wiki/Moorside,_Oldham" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorside, Oldham">Moorside</a>, exist as recently constructed residential <a href="/wiki/Suburbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Suburbia">suburbia</a>, whilst places like <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> exist as <a href="/wiki/Electoral_ward" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral ward">electoral wards</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and thoroughly industrialised districts. Throughout most of its <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>, Oldham was surrounded by large swathes of <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a>, which is reflected in the placenames of Moorside, <a href="/wiki/Greenacres,_Greater_Manchester" title="Greenacres, Greater Manchester">Greenacres moor</a>, Littlemoor, Northmoor among others.
</p><p>A large portion of Oldham's residences are "low value"<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> <a href="/wiki/Brick" title="Brick">Accrington red-brick</a> <a href="/wiki/Terraced_house" title="Terraced house">terraced houses</a> in a row formation,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> built for the most part from 1870 to 1920, to house the town's <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mill" title="Cotton mill">cotton mill</a> workers.<sup id="cite_ref-OSD_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSD-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> There is more modern housing in the semi-rural east of the town, in the most sought after area in areas such as the village <a href="/wiki/Moorside,_Oldham" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorside, Oldham">Moorside</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> although terraces are found in almost all parts of Oldham.
</p><p>One of the oldest recorded named places of Oldham is <a href="/wiki/Hathershaw" title="Hathershaw">Hathershaw</a>, occurring in a deed for 1280 with the spelling <i>Halselinechaw Clugh</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Existing as a manor in the 15th century, <a href="/wiki/Hathershaw_Hall" title="Hathershaw Hall">Hathershaw Hall</a> was the home of a <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalist</a> family in the 17th century who lost part of their possessions due to the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Waterhead,_Greater_Manchester" title="Waterhead, Greater Manchester">Waterhead</a>, an upland area in the east of Oldham, traces its roots to a water cornmill over the border in <a href="/wiki/Lees,_Greater_Manchester" title="Lees, Greater Manchester">Lees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaly1974_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaly1974-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recorded originally as <i>Watergate</i> and <i>Waterhead Milne</i>, it was for a long time a hamlet in the parish of Oldham that formed a significant part of the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Above_Town" title="Oldham Above Town">Oldham Above Town</a> registration sub-district. <a href="/wiki/Derker" title="Derker">Derker</a> was recorded as a place of residence in 1604 with the name <i>Dirtcar</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Bound by Higginshaw to the north, Derker is the location of <a href="/wiki/Derker_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Derker railway station">Derker railway station</a> and, said to have terraced residencies "unsuited to modern needs", is currently being redeveloped as part of the <a href="/wiki/Housing_Market_Renewal_Initiative" title="Housing Market Renewal Initiative">Housing Market Renewal Initiative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Coldhurst" title="Coldhurst">Coldhurst</a>, an area along Oldham's northern boundary with <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a>, was once a chapelry and the site of considerable industry and commerce, including <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">coal mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton_mills" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotton mills">cotton spinning</a> and hat manufacture.<sup id="cite_ref-VCH_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VCH-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> It is said to have been the scene of an action in the English Civil War in which the <a href="/wiki/Roundheads" class="mw-redirect" title="Roundheads">Parliamentarians</a> were defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-VCH_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VCH-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Greater_Manchester" title="Demography of Greater Manchester">Demography of Greater Manchester</a></div>
<table style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 0; font-size: 90%; border: 1px solid #aaa;">

<p>According to data from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">United Kingdom Census 2001</a>, Oldham had a total resident population of 103,544, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_England_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of urban areas in England by population">55th most populous settlement</a> in England, and the 5th most populous settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Urban_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Manchester Urban Area">Greater Manchester Urban Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Population_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Population-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This figure in conjunction with its area provides Oldham with a <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of 3,998 people per square mile (1,544&#160;per&#160;km²). The local population has been described as broadly "<a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a>"; the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle classes</a> tending to live in outlying settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham, considered as a combination of the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Ward_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (politics)">electoral wards</a> of Alexandra,<sup id="cite_ref-Alexandra_ward_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexandra_ward-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coldhurst" title="Coldhurst">Coldhurst</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Coldhurst_ward_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coldhurst_ward-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hollinwood_ward_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollinwood_ward-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> St. James,<sup id="cite_ref-James_ward_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_ward-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> St. Marys,<sup id="cite_ref-Mary_ward_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mary_ward-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> St. Pauls,<sup id="cite_ref-Paul_ward_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_ward-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Waterhead,_Greater_Manchester" title="Waterhead, Greater Manchester">Waterhead</a><sup id="cite_ref-Waterhead_ward_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waterhead_ward-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Werneth,_Greater_Manchester" title="Werneth, Greater Manchester">Werneth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Werneth_ward_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Werneth_ward-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> has an average age of 33.5, and compared against the average <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Demography of the United Kingdom">demography of the United Kingdom</a>, has a high level of people of <a href="/wiki/South_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="South Asian">South Asian</a> heritage, particularly those with roots in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. Due to the town's prevalence as an industrial centre and thus a hub for employment, Oldham attracted migrant workers throughout its history, including those from wider-England, Scotland, Ireland and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_People_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_People-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1950s and 1960s, in an attempt to fill the shortfall of workers and revitalise local industries, citizens of the wider <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> were encouraged to <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom_(1922-present_day)" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration to the United Kingdom (1922-present day)">migrate to Oldham and other British towns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_People_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_People-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Many came from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> and settled throughout the Oldham borough.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_People_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_People-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, Oldham has large communities with heritage from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, India, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and parts of the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_People_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_People-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> At the time of the 2001 census, over one in four of its residents identified themselves as from a South Asian or <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> ethnic group. Cultural divisions along ethnic backgrounds are strong within the town,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> with poor cross-community integration and cohesion along Asian and white backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With only a small local population during medieval times, as a result of the introduction of industry, mass migration of village workers into Oldham occurred,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a population change from under 2,000 in 1714<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButterworth1981-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> to 12,000 in 1801 to 137,000 in 1901<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000_18-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeilNevell2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1851 its population of 52,820 made Oldham the 12th most populous town in England.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_1907_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_1907-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The following is a table outlining the population change of the town since 1801, which demonstrates a trend of rapid population growth in the 19th century and, after peaking at 147,483 people in 1911, a trend of general decline in population size during the 20th century.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p>In 2011, 77.5% of the Oldham metropolitan borough population were White British, 18.1% Asian and 1.2% Black. While in the town of Oldham, which had a 2011 population of 96,555, 55.4% of the population were White British, 37.6% Asian and 2% Black.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg/220px-Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg/330px-Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg/440px-Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brian_Clarke_Spindles_Oldham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The stained glass roof of the Spindles, created by local artist Brian Clarke</div></div></div>
<p>For years Oldham's economy was heavily dependent on manufacturing industry, especially textiles and mechanical engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-Local_Company_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Local_Company-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Means_Business_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Means_Business-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Deindustrialisation">deindustrialisation</a> of Oldham in the mid-20th century, these industries have been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Home_shopping" title="Home shopping">home shopping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">publishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare">healthcare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a> sectors, though factory-generated employment retains a significant presence.<sup id="cite_ref-Local_Company_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Local_Company-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Many of the modern sectors are low-skill and low-wage.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park Cake Bakeries, sold in 2007 by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Foods" title="Northern Foods">Northern Foods Group</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vision_Capital" title="Vision Capital">Vision Capital</a>, have a large food processing centre in <a href="/wiki/Hathershaw" title="Hathershaw">Hathershaw</a>, which employs in excess of 1,600 people. Over 90% of the cakes produced go to <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Food_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Food-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Long existing as an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_district" title="Industrial district">industrial district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> is home to the Northern Counties Housing Association,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham's town centre contains the highest concentration of retailing, cultural facilities and employment in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It has been extensively redeveloped during the last few decades, and its two shopping centres, Town Square and the Spindles, now provide one of the largest covered retail areas in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Retail_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retail-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Spindles (named with reference to <a href="/wiki/Spindle_(textiles)" title="Spindle (textiles)">textile spindles</a>) is a modern <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping centre</a> with over 40 retailers, banks, building societies and catering outlets. It houses one of Europe's largest stained glass roofs, created by local artist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clarke_(artist)" title="Brian Clarke (artist)">Brian Clarke</a> in celebration of the music of one of Oldham's famous sons, <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conductor_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conductor (music)">conductor</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Walton" title="William Walton">William Walton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ferranti" title="Ferranti">Ferranti Technologies</a> is an electronic, electromechanical and electrical engineering company based in <a href="/wiki/Waterhead,_Greater_Manchester" title="Waterhead, Greater Manchester">Waterhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of culinary and medical advances have been developed in Oldham. There are claims that Oldham was the birthplace of the first <a href="/wiki/Fish_and_chips" title="Fish and chips">chip shop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chips_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chips-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The sometimes disputed claim of trade in deep-fried chipped potatoes is said to have been started around 1858–60 from an outlet owned by a John Lees, on what is the present site of Oldham's Tommyfield Market.<sup id="cite_ref-Chips_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chips-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In 1900 Oldham had the highest concentration of chip shops in the country, one for every 400 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Chips_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chips-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rag_Pudding" class="mw-redirect" title="Rag Pudding">Rag Pudding</a> is a savoury dish said to be native to Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yates_Wine_Lodge" class="mw-redirect" title="Yates Wine Lodge">Yates Wine Lodge</a> was founded in Oldham by Peter and Simon Yates in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClough1996_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClough1996-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bandage" title="Bandage">tubular bandage</a> was invented and developed in Oldham in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-Bandage_Bridge_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bandage_Bridge-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> That "vital contribution to advancing medical science" resulted from a collaboration between local firm Seton and a cotton manufacturer in the town.
</p><p>The majority of poor families are now working families.  Coldhurst in Oldham has child deprivation rate of 62.1pc, which is the worst in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic's</a> contribution to the local economy have been strengthened by its community links as well as its fortunes on the field. Despite some success in the early <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th century</a> which almost saw the club win the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> title in 1915, the club has spent most of its time outside the top division of English football, including a 68-year spell between 1923 and 1991 – when it won promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> a year before it became the <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>. The club then survived for three years in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>, which encouraged high attendances and boosted the club's finances as well as boosting the local economy as it struggled to recover from post-industrial decline. Between 1990 and 1994, the club also reached two FA Cup semi-finals (taking <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> to a replay on both occasions) and were on the losing side in a <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> final. The club's subsequent years, however, have been less successful, with relegation in 2018 to the fourth tier of the English league for the first time in almost 50 years.  The club's financial situation has also declined, as have its attendances, in accordance with fortunes on the pitch.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scheduled_Monuments_in_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Scheduled Monuments in Greater Manchester">List of Scheduled Monuments in Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grade_I_listed_buildings_in_Greater_Manchester" title="Grade I listed buildings in Greater Manchester">Grade I listed buildings in Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grade_II*_listed_buildings_in_Greater_Manchester" title="Grade II* listed buildings in Greater Manchester">Grade II* listed buildings in Greater Manchester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_art_in_Greater_Manchester" title="List of public art in Greater Manchester">List of public art in Greater Manchester</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg/220px-Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg/330px-Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg/440px-Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_Town_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oldham's old <a href="/wiki/Town_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Town hall">town hall</a>, built in 1841, in its disused state, before its recent conversion into a multiplex cinema</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_War_Memorial_(close_up).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg/220px-Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg/330px-Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg/440px-Oldham_War_Memorial_%28close_up%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_War_Memorial_(close_up).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oldham's war memorial was commissioned in 1919 to "symbolise the spirit of 1914–1918".</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg/220px-Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg/330px-Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg/440px-Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_Civic_Centre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The civic centre is the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a>'s centre of local governance.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_Hall">Town Hall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Town Hall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oldham's Old Town Hall is a Grade II listed <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neo-classical</a> <a href="/wiki/City_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="City hall">town hall</a> built in 1841,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> eight years before Oldham received its <a href="/wiki/Borough_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Borough status in the United Kingdom">borough status</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Town_Hall_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Town_Hall-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> One of the last purpose-built town halls in northwest England,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> it has a tetrastyle <a href="/wiki/Ionic_order" title="Ionic order">Ionic</a> <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">portico</a>, copied from the temple of <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(Roman_mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceres (Roman mythology)">Ceres</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Ilissos" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilissos">River Ilissos</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vision_of_Oldham_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_of_Oldham-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> made his inaugural acceptance speech from the steps of the town hall when he was first elected as a Conservative MP in 1900. A <a href="/wiki/Blue_Plaque" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Plaque">Blue Plaque</a> on the exterior of the building commemorates the event.<sup id="cite_ref-No_idea_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-No_idea-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Long existing as the political centre of the town, complete with <a href="/wiki/Courtroom" title="Courtroom">courtrooms</a>, the structure stood empty for many years from the mid-1980s and was regularly earmarked for redevelopment as part of regeneration project proposals, but none were actioned before plans dating to 2012 were completed in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Town_Hall_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Town_Hall-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-No_idea_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-No_idea-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2008, it was reported that "Oldham Town Hall is only months away from a major roof collapse".<sup id="cite_ref-Shame_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shame-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> A tour taken by local councillors and media concluded with an account that "chunks of masonry are falling from the ceilings on a daily basis&#160;... the floors are littered with dead pigeons and&#160;... revealed that the building is literally rotting away".<sup id="cite_ref-No_idea_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-No_idea-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shame_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shame-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In October 2009 the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Society">Victorian Society</a>, a charity responsible for the study and protection of Britain's Victorian and Edwardian architecture, declared Oldham Town Hall as the most endangered Victorian structure in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
Plans to convert the hall into a leisure complex, incorporating a cinema and restaurants, were revealed in May 2012 with the hall itself being used for public consultation.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> This £36.72 million project was completed in 2016.
</p><p>In the heart of Oldham's retail district, the Old Town Hall has been developed into a modern multiplex <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinemas" title="Odeon Cinemas">Odeon cinema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_memorial">War memorial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: War memorial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oldham_War_Memorial" title="Oldham War Memorial">Oldham War Memorial</a></div>
<p>Erected as a permanent memorial to the men of Oldham who were killed in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, Oldham's <a href="/wiki/War_memorial" title="War memorial">war memorial</a> consists of a <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> base surmounted by a <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a> sculpture depicting five soldiers making their way along the trenches in order to go into battle.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_War_Memorial_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_War_Memorial-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The main standing figure, having climbed out of the trenches, is shown calling on his comrades to advance, and is the same figure used at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fusiliers_War_Memorial" title="Royal Fusiliers War Memorial">Royal Fusiliers War Memorial</a> in London and the <a href="/wiki/41st_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="41st Division (United Kingdom)">41st Division</a> memorial at <a href="/wiki/Flers,_Somme" title="Flers, Somme">Flers</a> in France. The base serves to house books containing the roll of honour of the 1st, 10th and 24th Battalions, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Regiment" title="Manchester Regiment">Manchester Regiment</a>. The pedestal has two bronze doors at either side.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_War_Memorial_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_War_Memorial-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Commissioned in 1919 by the Oldham War Memorial Committee, the memorial was designed and built by <a href="/wiki/Albert_Toft" title="Albert Toft">Albert Toft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> It was unveiled by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Standish_Monteith_Hamilton" class="mw-redirect" title="Ian Standish Monteith Hamilton">General Sir Ian Hamilton</a> on 28 April 1923, before a crowd estimated at over 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_War_Memorial_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_War_Memorial-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The monument was intended to symbolise the spirit of 1914–1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The inscriptions on the memorial read:
</p>
<ul><li>Over doors to the north:  "DEATH IS THE GATE OF LIFE / 1914–1918"</li>
<li>Over window to the south: "TO GOD BE THE PRAISE "</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_Centre">Civic Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Civic Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Civic Centre tower is the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a>'s centre of local governance. The 15-storey white-brick building has housed the vast majority of the local government's offices since its completion in 1977. Standing at the summit of the town, the tower stands over 200 feet (61&#160;m) high.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> It was designed by Cecil Howitt &amp; Partners,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Topping_out" title="Topping out">topping out</a> ceremony was held on 18 June 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillett1996_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillett1996-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Civic Centre can be seen as far away as <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trafford" title="Trafford">Trafford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wythenshawe" title="Wythenshawe">Wythenshawe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winter_Hill_(Lancashire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Hill (Lancashire)">Winter Hill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>, and offers panoramic views across the city of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cheshire_Plain" title="Cheshire Plain">Cheshire Plain</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parish_Church">Parish Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Parish Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_churches_in_Greater_Manchester" title="List of churches in Greater Manchester">List of churches in Greater Manchester</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Parish_Church" title="Oldham Parish Church">Oldham Parish Church of St. Mary with St. Peter</a>, in its present form, dates from 1830 and was designed in the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival Style</a> by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lane_(architect)" title="Richard Lane (architect)">Richard Lane</a>, a Manchester-based architect.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It has been designated by <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a> as a Grade II* <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> It was linked with the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Mary_the_Virgin,_Prestwich" title="Church of St Mary the Virgin, Prestwich">church of St Mary the Virgin, Prestwich</a> and together the sites were principal churches of the ancient ecclesiastical parish of <a href="/wiki/Prestwich-cum-Oldham" title="Prestwich-cum-Oldham">Prestwich-cum-Oldham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A church building had existed on the site since 1280.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> During this time, a small chapel stood on the site to serve the local townships of Oldham, <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaw_and_Crompton" title="Shaw and Crompton">Crompton</a>. This was later replaced by an <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Early English Gothic</a> church in the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> With the coming of the Industrial Revolution, the population of Oldham increased at a rapid rate (from under 2,000 in 1714, to over 32,000 by 1831).<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The rapid growth of the local population warranted that the building be rebuilt into the current structure. Though the budget was originally agreed at £5,000,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> the final cost of building was £30,000, one third of which was spent on the crypt structure.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Alternative designs by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_Barry" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Charles Barry">Sir Charles Barry</a>, the designer of the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a>, although now regarded by some as superior, were rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The Church, of the <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> denomination, is in active use for worship, and forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Manchester" title="Anglican Diocese of Manchester">Diocese of Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Parish_Church1_74-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parish_Church1-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> There are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> churches in Oldham. These include <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel_and_St_Patrick_Church,_Oldham" title="Our Lady of Mount Carmel and St Patrick Church, Oldham">Our Lady of Mount Carmel and St Patrick Church</a>. It was built in 1870, was founded by priests from St Mary's Church in Oldham, and is a Grade II listed building.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bus_in_Oldham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bus_in_Oldham.jpg/220px-Bus_in_Oldham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bus_in_Oldham.jpg/330px-Bus_in_Oldham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bus_in_Oldham.jpg/440px-Bus_in_Oldham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bus_in_Oldham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 409 to <a href="/wiki/Rochdale" title="Rochdale">Rochdale</a>, pictured in Oldham's town centre. <a href="/wiki/First_Greater_Manchester" title="First Greater Manchester">First Greater Manchester</a> has its headquarters in Oldham, operating bus services throughout Greater Manchester.</div></div></div>
<p>The geography of Oldham constrained the development of major transport infrastructure,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_1907_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_1907-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> with the former County Borough Council suggesting that "if it had not grown substantially before the railway age it would surely have been overlooked".<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_1907_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_1907-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Oldham has never been on a main-line railway route, and canals too have only been able to serve it from a distance,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_1907_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_1907-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> meaning that "Oldham has never had a train service worthy of a town of its size".<sup id="cite_ref-Chadderton_1907_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chadderton_1907-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A principal destination along the former <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Loop_Line" title="Oldham Loop Line">Oldham Loop Line</a>, Oldham once had six <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway stations</a> but this was reduced to three once <a href="/wiki/Clegg_Street_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Clegg Street railway station">Clegg Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Central_railway_station" title="Oldham Central railway station">Oldham Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glodwick_Road_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glodwick Road railway station">Glodwick Road</a> closed in the mid-20th century. <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Werneth_railway_station" title="Oldham Werneth railway station">Oldham Werneth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Mumps_railway_station" title="Oldham Mumps railway station">Oldham Mumps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derker_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Derker railway station">Derker</a> closed on 3 October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-sig_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sig-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-era_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-era-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Trains from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station" title="Manchester Victoria station">Manchester Victoria station</a> to Oldham had to climb steeply through much of its 6-mile (9.7&#160;km) route, from around 100 feet (30.5&#160;m) at Manchester city centre to around 600 feet (182.9&#160;m) at Oldham Mumps.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_1907_75-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_1907-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The Werneth Incline, with its gradient of 1 in 27, made the <a href="/wiki/Middleton_Junction_railway_station" title="Middleton Junction railway station">Middleton Junction</a> to <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Werneth_railway_station" title="Oldham Werneth railway station">Oldham Werneth</a> route the steepest regular passenger line in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Chadderton_1907_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chadderton_1907-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Werneth Incline route closed in 1963. It had been replaced as the main route to Manchester by the section of line built between Oldham Werneth Station and Thorpes Bridge Junction, at <a href="/wiki/Newton_Heath" title="Newton Heath">Newton Heath</a> in May 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Oldham Mumps, the second oldest station on the line after Werneth,<sup id="cite_ref-sig_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sig-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> took its name from its location in the Mumps area of Oldham, which itself probably derived from the archaic word "mumper" which was slang for a <a href="/wiki/Beggar" class="mw-redirect" title="Beggar">beggar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibb200528_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibb200528-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The former Oldham Loop Line was converted for use with an expanded <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> light rail network, and renamed as the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_and_Rochdale_Line" title="Oldham and Rochdale Line">Oldham and Rochdale Line</a>. The line between Victoria and a temporary <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Mumps_tram_stop" title="Oldham Mumps tram stop">Oldham Mumps tram stop</a> opened on 13 June 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sig_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sig-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-era_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-era-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and more central stops opened on 27 January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham had electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramways</a> to Manchester in the early 20th century; the first tram was driven from Manchester into Oldham in 1900 by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lord_Mayors_of_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Lord Mayors of Manchester">Lord Mayor of Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillett1996_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillett1996-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The system came to an end on 3 August 1946, however.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>  There was also a short-lived <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Oldham" title="Trolleybuses in Oldham">Oldham trolleybus system</a>, in 1925–26.  The £3.3 million <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Bus_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldham Bus Station">Oldham Bus Station</a> has frequent bus services to Manchester, Rochdale, Ashton-under-Lyne and Middleton with other services to the Metropolitan Borough of Oldham, <a href="/wiki/Tameside" title="Tameside">Tameside</a>, and across the Pennines to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Bus_Station_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Bus_Station-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The roof canopy is supported internally on two rows of steel trees. The extensive use of glass and stainless steel maximises visibility, and there is a carefully co-ordinated family of information fittings, posters and seating, using robust natural materials for floors and plinths.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Bus_Station_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Bus_Station-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The bus station is used by <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> coaches. <a href="/wiki/First_Greater_Manchester" title="First Greater Manchester">First Greater Manchester</a> has its headquarters in Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the Turnpike Act 1734, Oldham had no turnpike road to Manchester for another 56 years and <a href="/wiki/Church_Lane,_Oldham" title="Church Lane, Oldham">Church Lane, Oldham</a> remained part of the main street through the town. But following a further Act of Parliament a turnpike was constructed. The first regular coach service to Manchester came into operation in October 1790, with a journey time of over 2 hours and a fare 2s.8d (about 13p), with half fare for travellers on top of the coach.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham is about 4 miles (6.4&#160;km) south of the major <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62 motorway</a>, but is linked to it by the <a href="/wiki/M60_motorway" title="M60 motorway">M60</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/A627(M)_motorway" title="A627(M) motorway">A627(M)</a> via <a href="/wiki/Chadderton" title="Chadderton">Chadderton</a>. There are major <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">A roads</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ashton-under-Lyne" title="Ashton-under-Lyne">Ashton-under-Lyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rochdale" title="Rochdale">Rochdale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood_Branch_Canal" title="Hollinwood Branch Canal">Hollinwood Branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ashton_Canal" title="Ashton Canal">Ashton Canal</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Canals of Great Britain">canal</a> that ran from <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Droylsden" class="mw-redirect" title="Fairfield, Droylsden">Fairfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/Droylsden" title="Droylsden">Droylsden</a>, through Littlemoss and <a href="/wiki/Daisy_Nook" title="Daisy Nook">Daisy Nook Country Park</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Hollinwood,_Greater_Manchester" title="Hollinwood, Greater Manchester">Hollinwood</a> area of Oldham, with a branch from Daisy Nook to the <a href="/wiki/Fairbottom_Branch_Canal" title="Fairbottom Branch Canal">Fairbottom Branch Canal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The canal was mainly used for the haulage of <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> until it fell into disuse for commercial traffic in the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> It included four aqueducts and a two-rise lock staircase.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boundary_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Boundary_Park.jpg/220px-Boundary_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Boundary_Park.jpg/330px-Boundary_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Boundary_Park.jpg/440px-Boundary_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2987" data-file-height="1131" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boundary_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boundary_Park" title="Boundary Park">Boundary Park</a> is Oldham's main sports stadium, and is used by <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic A.F.C.</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham R.L.F.C.</a> Rugby League Club was established in 1876 as Oldham Football Club,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic Association Football Club</a> in 1895 as Pine Villa Football Club. Oldham Athletic have achieved both league and cup successes, particularly under <a href="/wiki/Joe_Royle" title="Joe Royle">Joe Royle</a> in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Beyond_27-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Beyond-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> They were <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/1914%E2%80%9315_in_English_football" title="1914–15 in English football">last season before the outbreak</a> of the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, but were relegated from the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Football League First Division</a> in 1923. They reached the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> final in 1990 and won the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Football League Second Division</a> title in 1991, ending 68&#160;years outside the top flight.
</p><p>They secured their top division status a year later to become founder members of the new <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bandage_Bridge_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bandage_Bridge-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> but were relegated after <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_in_English_football" title="1993–94 in English football">two seasons</a> despite reaching that year's <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-finals.  They are currently playing in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Two">Football League Two</a>, the fourth tier of the English league.
</p><p>Oldham netball club's senior team is the 2019 national league division 1 champion and has won seven out of the last eight titles. Former players include England's most capped player <a href="/wiki/Jade_Clarke" title="Jade Clarke">Jade Clarke</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Oldham_Borough_F.C." title="Oldham Borough F.C.">Oldham Borough</a> was established in 1964 as Oldham Dew FC, and after many years playing under the name of <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldham Town">Oldham Town</a> changed its name to Oldham Boro in 2009, finally becoming known as Oldham Borough just months before it folded. The team played in the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Counties_Football_League" title="North West Counties Football League">North West Counties Football League</a> before going out of existence in 2015, just over 50 years after it was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Renamed in 1997 to <a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham R.L.F.C.</a>, Oldham Rugby League Club has received several club honours during its history,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Rugby_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Rugby-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> winning the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Football League Championship">Rugby Football League Championship</a> five times and <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> three times.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Rugby_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Rugby-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> They played at <a href="/wiki/Watersheddings" title="Watersheddings">Watersheddings</a> for years before joining Oldham Athletic at <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Park" title="Boundary Park">Boundary Park</a> until 2010 when they moved to Oldham Borough's previous ground, <a href="/wiki/Whitebank_Stadium" title="Whitebank Stadium">Whitebank Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Rugby_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Rugby-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Oldham has league cricket teams with a number of semi-professional league clubs including <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Cricket_Club" title="Oldham Cricket Club">Oldham CC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Werneth_Cricket_Club" title="Werneth Cricket Club">Werneth CC</a> in the Central Lancashire League.
</p><p>Oldham also has a Fencing Club, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshall_Fencing_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marshall Fencing Club (page does not exist)">Marshall Fencing Club</a> is a Competitive Fencing Club with most of its members competing on the national stage.
They train three times a week at the old South Chadderton High School.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Oldham" title="List of schools in Oldham">List of schools in Oldham</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_College.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_College.jpg/220px-Oldham_College.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_College.jpg/330px-Oldham_College.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Oldham_College.jpg/440px-Oldham_College.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1540" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oldham_College.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oldham_College" title="Oldham College">Oldham College</a> is a centre for <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_coat0004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Blue_coat0004.jpg/220px-Blue_coat0004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Blue_coat0004.jpg/330px-Blue_coat0004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Blue_coat0004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="253" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_coat0004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Coat_School,_Oldham" title="The Blue Coat School, Oldham">The Blue Coat School</a> is one of Oldham's oldest schools, dating back to 1834.</div></div></div>
<p>Oldham produced someone who is considered<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Evolution_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Evolution-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> to be one of the greatest benefactors of education for the nation, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Oldham" title="Hugh Oldham">Hugh Oldham</a>, who in 1504 was appointed as <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Exeter" title="Bishop of Exeter">Bishop of Exeter</a>, and later went on to found what is now <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Grammar_School" title="Manchester Grammar School">Manchester Grammar School</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/University_Campus_Oldham" class="mw-redirect" title="University Campus Oldham">University Campus Oldham</a> is a centre for <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> and a sister campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">University of Huddersfield</a>. It was opened in May 2005 by actor <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a>, the centre's Chancellor.<sup id="cite_ref-UCO_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCO-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The University Campus Oldham presented actress <a href="/wiki/Shobna_Gulati" title="Shobna Gulati">Shobna Gulati</a> and artist, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clarke_(artist)" title="Brian Clarke (artist)">Brian Clarke</a> (both born in Oldham) with an <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Letters" title="Doctor of Letters">Honorary Doctorate of Letters</a> at the Graduation Ceremony of November 2006, for their achievements and contributions to Oldham and its community.<sup id="cite_ref-UCO_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCO-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
