<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> policing in Oldham is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Police" title="Greater Manchester Police">Greater Manchester Police</a>. The force's "(Q) Division" have their headquarters for policing the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Oldham" title="Metropolitan Borough of Oldham">Metropolitan Borough of Oldham</a> at central Oldham. <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">Public transport</a> is co-ordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Passenger_Transport_Executive" title="Greater Manchester Passenger Transport Executive">Greater Manchester Passenger Transport Executive</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fire_service_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire service in the United Kingdom">Statutory emergency fire and rescue service</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Greater Manchester Fire and Rescue Service">Greater Manchester Fire and Rescue Service</a>, which has two stations in Oldham; at Hollins on Hollins Road,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> and at Clarksfield on Lees Road.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Oldham_Hospital" title="Royal Oldham Hospital">Royal Oldham Hospital</a>, at Oldham's northern boundary with <a href="/wiki/Royton" title="Royton">Royton</a>, is a large <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">NHS</a> hospital administrated by <a href="/wiki/Pennine_Acute_Hospitals_NHS_Trust" title="Pennine Acute Hospitals NHS Trust">Pennine Acute Hospitals NHS Trust</a>. It was opened under its existing name on 1 December 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-Workhouse_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Workhouse-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Formerly known as Oldham District and General, and occupying the site of the town's former <a href="/wiki/Workhouse" title="Workhouse">workhouse</a> (named Oldham Union Workhouse in 1851),<sup id="cite_ref-Workhouse_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Workhouse-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> the hospital is notable for being the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Louise_Joy_Brown" class="mw-redirect" title="Louise Joy Brown">Louise Joy Brown</a>&#160;– the world's first successful <a href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation" title="In vitro fertilisation"><i>In vitro</i> fertilised "test tube baby"</a>, on 25 July 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-Test_Tube_Baby_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Test_Tube_Baby-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">Waste management</a> is co-ordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Local_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local authority">local authority</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Waste_Disposal_Authority" title="Greater Manchester Waste Disposal Authority">Greater Manchester Waste Disposal Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Locally produced <a href="/wiki/Inert_waste" title="Inert waste">inert waste</a> for disposal is sent to <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a> at the Beal Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Oldham's <a href="/wiki/Distribution_Network_Operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Distribution Network Operator">Distribution Network Operator</a> for electricity is <a href="/wiki/United_Utilities" title="United Utilities">United Utilities</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-UU_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UU-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> there are no <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power stations</a> in the town. United Utilities also manages Oldham's <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waste_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Waste water">waste water</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-UU_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UU-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> water supplies being sourced from several local reservoirs, including <a href="/wiki/Dovestones_Reservoir" class="mw-redirect" title="Dovestones Reservoir">Dovestones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chew_Reservoir,_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Chew Reservoir, Greater Manchester">Chew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> There is a <a href="/wiki/Water_treatment" title="Water treatment">water treatment</a> works at <a href="/wiki/Waterhead,_Greater_Manchester" title="Waterhead, Greater Manchester">Waterhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UU_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UU-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Oldham, though lacking in leisure and cultural amenities,<sup id="cite_ref-Rebrand_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebrand-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> is historically notable for its theatrical culture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1986_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1986-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Once having a peak of six <i>"fine"</i> theatres in 1908,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1986_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1986-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Oldham is home to the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Coliseum_Theatre" title="Oldham Coliseum Theatre">Oldham Coliseum Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Theatre_Workshop" title="Oldham Theatre Workshop">Oldham Theatre Workshop</a>, which have facilitated the early careers of notable actors and writers, including <a href="/wiki/Eric_Sykes" title="Eric Sykes">Eric Sykes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1986_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1986-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Cribbins" title="Bernard Cribbins">Bernard Cribbins</a><sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Career1_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Career1-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Kirkbride" title="Anne Kirkbride">Anne Kirkbride</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Career1_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Career1-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> daughter of acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Cartoonist" title="Cartoonist">cartoonist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kirkbride" title="Jack Kirkbride">Jack Kirkbride</a> who worked for the <i><a href="/wiki/Oldham_Evening_Chronicle" title="Oldham Evening Chronicle">Oldham Evening Chronicle</a></i>. Oldham Coliseum Theatre is one of Britain's last remaining <a href="/wiki/Repertory_theatre" title="Repertory theatre">repertory theatres</a>; <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stan_Laurel" title="Stan Laurel">Stan Laurel</a> performed there in the early 20th century, and contemporary actors such as <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Fiennes" title="Ralph Fiennes">Ralph Fiennes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Driver" title="Minnie Driver">Minnie Driver</a>, among others, have appeared more recently.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlewellin2000_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlewellin2000-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> A notable home grown musical act is The <a href="/wiki/Blackout_Crew" title="Blackout Crew">Blackout Crew</a>.
</p><p>During the 19th century the <a href="/wiki/Circus" title="Circus">circus</a> was a popular entertainment in Oldham; <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Fanque" title="Pablo Fanque">Pablo Fanque</a>'s circus was a regular visitor, filling a 3,000-seat amphitheatre on Tommyfield in 1869.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>  Formerly criticised for its lack of a <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">cinema</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Rebrand_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebrand-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> there are plans to develop an "Oldham <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-West_End_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_End-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Oldham has a thriving bar and <a href="/wiki/Night_club" class="mw-redirect" title="Night club">night club</a> culture, attracting a significant number of young people into the town centre.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Oldham's "hard <a href="/wiki/Binge_drinking" title="Binge drinking">binge drinking</a> culture" has been criticised however for conveying a negative regional image of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-Rebrand_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebrand-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communal_facilities">Communal facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Communal facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg/220px-The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg/330px-The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg/440px-The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Lyceum_and_Science_%26_Art_Building._-_geograph.org.uk_-_493742.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Lyceum is a Grade II listed building opened in 1856 as a "mutual improvement" centre for the working men of Oldham.</div></div></div>
<p>The Lyceum is a <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">Grade II listed building</a><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> opened in 1856 at a cost of £6,500 as a "mutual improvement" centre for the working men of Oldham.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The facilities provided to members included a library, a newsroom and a series of lectures on geology, geography and education, microscopy and chemistry, female education and botany.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Lyceum_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Lyceum-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Instrumental music was introduced and there were soon sixteen violinists and three cellists. Eventually the building was extended to include a school of science and art. Music had always been important in the life of the Lyceum, and in 1892 a school of music was opened, with 39 students enrolled for the "theory and practice of music".
</p><p>The Lyceum continued throughout the 20th century as a centre for the arts in Oldham, and in 1986 the local authority was invited by its directors and trustees to accept the building as a gift.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Lyceum_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Lyceum-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The acceptance of the Lyceum building by the Education Committee provided the opportunity to move the music centre and "further enhance the cultural activities of the town".<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Lyceum_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Lyceum-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 the Oldham Metropolitan Borough Music Centre moved into the Lyceum building, which is now the home of the Oldham Lyceum School of Music.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Lyceum_141-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Lyceum-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham's museum and gallery service dates back to 1883.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallery_Oldham_1_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallery_Oldham_1-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Since then it has established itself as a cultural focus for Oldham and has developed one of the largest and most varied permanent collections in <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West England</a>. The current collection includes over 12,000 social and industrial history items, more than 2,000 works of art, about 1,000 items of decorative art, more than 80,000 natural history specimens, over 1,000 geological specimens, about 3,000 archaeological artefacts, 15,000 photographs and a large number of books, pamphlets and documents.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallery_Oldham_1_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallery_Oldham_1-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Rifle_Street_drill_hall,_Oldham" title="Rifle Street drill hall, Oldham">Rifle Street drill hall</a> dates back to 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oldham is now home to a newly built state-of-the-art art gallery, <a href="/wiki/Gallery_Oldham" title="Gallery Oldham">Gallery Oldham</a>, which was completed in February 2002 as the first phase of the Oldham Cultural Quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallery_Oldham_2_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallery_Oldham_2-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Later phases of the development saw the opening of an extended Oldham Library, a lifelong learning centre and there are plans to include a performing arts centre.<sup id="cite_ref-Oldham_Heart_7-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oldham_Heart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carnival">Carnival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Carnival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The annual Oldham Carnival started around 1900, although the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnivals</a> in the town goes back much further, providing a "welcomed respite from the tedium of everyday life".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The carnival parade was always held in mid-to-late summer, with the primary aim of raising money for charities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> It often featured local dignitaries or popular entertainers, in addition to brass, military and jazz bands, the Carnival Queen, people in <a href="/wiki/Fancy_dress" class="mw-redirect" title="Fancy dress">fancy dress</a>, dancers and decorated <a href="/wiki/Float_(parade)" title="Float (parade)">floats</a> from local churches and businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Whenever possible, local people who had attained national celebrity status were invited to join the cavalcade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The carnival's route began in the town centre, wound its way along King Street, and ended with a party in <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Park,_Oldham" title="Alexandra Park, Oldham">Alexandra Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005_145-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrummond2005-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The carnival fell out of favour in the late 1990s but was resurrected by community volunteers in 2006 and rebranded the Peoples' Carnival. The parade was moved into Alexandra Park in 2011. The event hosts live stages and other activities alongside a parade in the park.<sup id="cite_ref-Todays_Carnival_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todays_Carnival-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carnival_History_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnival_History-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> 2016 marked ten years since the carnival was reinstated by volunteers. The main organiser is Paul Davies who runs the carnival with a number of committee members and volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain_in_Bloom">Britain in Bloom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Britain in Bloom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2012 and 2014 Oldham was named as Culture Town in the annual "Britain in Bloom" competition as winners. It also won the North West in bloom competition, winning the Oldham Council trophy. Oldham council financially support the rewards program.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oldham&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Oldham" title="List of people from Oldham">List of people from Oldham</a></div>
<p>People from Oldham are called Oldhamers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClough1996_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClough1996-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> though "Roughyed" is a <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">nickname</a> from the 18th century when rough <a href="/wiki/Felt" title="Felt">felt</a> was used in Oldham to make hats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBateson1949_11-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBateson1949-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Potts_(architect)" title="Edward Potts (architect)">Edward Potts</a> was a renowned architect who moved to Oldham from <a href="/wiki/Bury,_Greater_Manchester" title="Bury, Greater Manchester">Bury</a>. He was the architect for fourteen mills in the Oldham area.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other notable persons with Oldham connections include the composer Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Walton" title="William Walton">William Walton</a>, former British Prime Minister Sir <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Louise_Brown" title="Louise Brown">Louise Brown</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Test_Tube_Baby_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Test_Tube_Baby-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> the world's first baby to be conceived by <a href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation" title="In vitro fertilisation"><i>in vitro</i> fertilisation</a>.
</p><p>Notable media personalities from Oldham include presenter <a href="/wiki/Nick_Grimshaw" title="Nick Grimshaw">Nick Grimshaw</a>, actors <a href="/wiki/Eric_Sykes" title="Eric Sykes">Eric Sykes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Cribbins" title="Bernard Cribbins">Bernard Cribbins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Biggins" title="Christopher Biggins">Christopher Biggins</a>, TV host <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Schofield" title="Phillip Schofield">Phillip Schofield</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bandage_Bridge_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bandage_Bridge-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> actress <a href="/wiki/Shobna_Gulati" title="Shobna Gulati">Shobna Gulati</a>, actress/comedian <a href="/wiki/Dora_Bryan" title="Dora Bryan">Dora Bryan</a>, actress <a href="/wiki/Anne_Kirkbride" title="Anne Kirkbride">Anne Kirkbride</a>, physicist and science educator <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a>, and comedy double act <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Cannon" title="Tommy Cannon">Tommy Cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Ball" title="Bobby Ball">Bobby Ball</a>.
</p><p>Notable musicians from Oldham include the <a href="/wiki/Inspiral_Carpets" title="Inspiral Carpets">Inspiral Carpets</a>, <a href="/wiki/N-Trance" title="N-Trance">N-Trance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Owen" title="Mark Owen">Mark Owen</a> of boyband <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> as well as the founding members of the rock band <a href="/wiki/Barclay_James_Harvest" title="Barclay James Harvest">Barclay James Harvest</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a> (32 &amp; 33 Vict. c.49) s.31 <i>"Each of the boroughs named in the Third Schedule to this Act being a borough which on the first day of June one thousand eight hundred and eighty-eight, either had a population of not less than fifty thousand, or was a county of itself shall, from and after the appointed day, be for the purposes of this Act an administrative county of itself, and is in this Act referred to as a county borough. Provided that for all other purposes a county borough shall continue to be part of the county (if any) in which it is situate at the passing of this Act"</i></span>
